IN THE SUPREME COURT OF INDIA 
CIVIL APPELLATE JURISDICTION 
 
CIVIL APPEAL NO……………………. OF 2026 
(@ Special Leave Petition (Civil)No.15867 of 2026) 
 
RAMSHAD P                           ... APPELLANT(S) 
  
VERSUS 
 
AFSAL & ORS.             ... RESPONDENT(S)    
                 
 
O R D E R 
 
Time taken for 
disposal of the 
claim petition by 
the MACT 
Time taken for 
disposal of 
appeal by the 
High Court 
Time taken for 
the disposal of 
the appeal in 
this Court 
5 years, 2 months, 
19 days 
1 year, 1 month, 
9 days 
2 months, 13 days 
 
 
  Leave granted. 
2.   This appeal arises from a motor vehicle accident 
that occurred on 21.05.2017. The appellant, then a 20 -
year-old youth, was traveling in a car (Reg. No. KL-08-
AS-9970) which, due to the rash and negligent driving of 

--- Page 23 ---
2 
 
Respondent No. 2, overturned into a valley. The appellant 
sustained catastrophic spinal injuries, including C6-C7 
spondylolisthesis and cervical cord injury, resulting in 
100% permanent disability  with the claimant being 
permanent bedridden. He is currently in a paraplegic 
condition, suffering from total incontinence and is 
entirely dependent on others for his daily survival. 
3. The Motor Accident Claims Tribunal, Thrissur, on 
19.08.2023, awarded a total compensation of ₹64,71,050/- 
with interest at the rate of 7.5% per annum from the date 
of the petition until realization. 
4. Upon appeal (MACA No. 1096 of 2024), the High Court 
of Kerala enhanced the compensation by an additional 
₹28,52,400/-, bringing the total award to ₹93,23,450/-. 
The High Court further directed that the compensation be 
paid with a revised interest rate of 8 % per annum from 
the date of the petition till realization. 
5. The High Court refixed the petitioner's notional 
income at ₹13,000/ - per month. However, taking into 
account the minimum wages payable to skilled workmen in 
the State of Kerala as of the date of the accident 
(21.05.2017), we refix the notional monthly inco me at 

--- Page 24 ---
3 
 
₹18,900/-. Herein we may extract the relevant portion of 
the decision rendered by the High Court of Kerala, 
acknowledging the minimum wages payable to a skilled 
worker in the year 2018, which were also prevalent with 
effect from 28.04.2017, prior to the accident in 
question. 
“In the present case, the accident occurred 
on 24.04.2018 and at that point of time, 
G.O.(P) No. 56/2017 dated 28.04.2017 issued 
by the State of Kerala was in force.  In 
accordance with the said notification, the 
minimum wage fixed by the State of Kerala for 
a skilled worker is at Rs. 18,900/ -.  
Therefore, the compensation towards loss of 
dependency has to be reworked.” 
 
Hence, compensation for loss of future earnings needs to 
be recalculated accordingly, maintaining the 40% addition 
for future prospects and the multiplier of 18. 
6. The Motor Accident Claims Tribunal (MACT), Thrissur, 
after assessing the police records and FIR in Crime No. 
362/2017, held that the accident was the result of the 
negligence of the driver of the offending vehicle. As 
the vehicle was covered by a valid insurance policy, the 
Tribunal fastened the liability solely upon the insurer, 
The New India Assurance Co. Ltd. (Respondent No. 3), to 

--- Page 25 ---
4 
 
indemnify the owner. This finding on liability was not 
challenged and has attained finality. 
7. While the High Court enhanced the compensation to 
₹93,23,450/-, we find the assessment of several heads 
remains inadequate to meet the standard of "just 
compensation" for a claimant in such a state of perpetual 
suffering.  
8. Based on the aforementioned findings, the final 
compensation is re-calculated as follows:

1. Mr.  B.  Karunakaran,  learned  Advocate-on-

2. Delay condoned. Leave granted. 
3. This appeal by way of special leave is
against the order of the High Court of Judicature
at  Madras  dated  06.11.2025  by  which  the
appellant’s application for regular bail bearing
Crl. O.P. No. 25241 of 2025 has been dismissed.
 
Crl. Appeal @ SLP (Crl) @ D.No. 31184 of 2026       1

--- Page 30 ---
4. The appellant was arrested on 04.06.2025 in
connection  with  FIR  No.  387/2025   dated
04.06.2025  registered  at  P.S.  R.K.  Nagar,
District Washermenpet for the offences punishable
under Sections 8(c), 22(c) and 29(1) of the
Narcotic Drugs and Psychotropic Substances Act,
1985.
5. Heard  learned  counsel  appearing  for  the
parties. 
6. We  note  from  the  FIR/seizure  list  that
recovery of 700 grams of methamphetamine was from
the appellant and co-accused. Co-accused have
been released on bail. Learned counsel for the
appellant contends that he stands on same footing
with the co-accused which is seriously contested
by the learned counsel for the respondent-State.
Learned  counsel  for  respondent-State  contends
that the appellant is the principal accused and
recovery was made from him. He also submits that
there  are  money  transactions  between  the
appellant and others with regard to the illicit
 
Crl. Appeal @ SLP (Crl) @ D.No. 31184 of 2026       2

--- Page 31 ---
dealing in narcotics. 
7. Having considered the materials on record,
particularly  the  FIR/seizure  list  evidencing
joint recovery, we are of the opinion that the
appellant  substantially  stands  on  the  same
footing with co-accused who have been enlarged on
bail.  In  these  circumstances,  we  allow  the
appeal, set aside the order rejecting bail and
direct that the appellant shall be released on
bail on same terms and conditions as that of the
co-accused.

IN THE SUPREME COURT OF INDIA
CIVIL APPELLATE JURISDICTION
CIVIL APPEAL NO.________/2024
(@ SPECIAL LEAVE PETITION (CIVIL) NO.6056/2018)
M/S POLICE CITY HOUSING COOPERATIVE 
SOCIETY LIMITED   APPELLANT(S)
                           VERSUS
THE ADDITIONAL COMMISSIONER (IIIRD) 
MEERUT & ORS.    RESPONDENT(S)
O R D E R
1. Leave granted.
2. Heard the learned counsel appearing for the parties.
3. The proceedings arise out of determination of market
value and deficiency in stamp duty under Section 47-A of the
Indian Stamp Act, 1899, (for short, ‘The Act’) as amended in
the State of Uttar Pradesh with respect to the land under the
sale deed in question.  The appellant, which is a Cooperative
Society, had purchased 2043 square meter of agricultural
land.  According to the circle rate prescribed by the
Collector under Rule 341 of the Indian Stamp Rules, 1997 the
rate for residential plots was Rs.4,000/- per square meter
where it was abutting the road and Rs.2,000/- per square
meter which was away from the road and in the village.
According to the appellant, the sale deed in question was for

--- Page 45 ---
2
a total consideration of Rs.63,96,000/- on which due stamp
duty was paid.  As per the sale consideration, the rate of
the land would come to about Rs.3157/- per square meter.  The
proceedings under the Act were initiated for considering
whether the instrument has been correctly valued and due
stamp duty has been paid or not.  In the said proceedings,
the Collector applied the rate of Rs.4,000 per square meter
treating the land to be on the main road, vide order dated
31st March, 2008 and accordingly levied deficiency in stamp
duty as Rs.1,72,200/- and further penalty and statutory
interest amounting to Rs.6,88,000/- was also imposed making
the total of Rs.8,60,200/- to be paid by the appellant.
4. The said order was carried unsuccessfully in revision
and thereafter before the High Court where the writ petition
was dismissed by the impugned order dated 12 th December,
2017.  
5. According to the learned counsel appearing for the
appellant, neither the Collector nor any of the superior
authorities or the High Court recorded a finding that the
land purchased under the sale deed in question was situated
on the main road.  His further submission is that there was
enough material on record before the Collector by way of
reports of the officials of the Revenue Department, the
revenue map and other evidence to show that the land was away
from the main road and therefore, the rate applicable would

--- Page 46 ---
3
be Rs.2,000/- per square meter.  The appellant having already
paid stamp duty at a higher  rate of Rs.3157/- per square
meter, the order imposing deficiency, in penalty and interest
are unsustainable in law.
6. We have examined the impugned orders and find that there
is no such discussion of the material on record or even a
finding recorded that the land in question was situated on
the main road based on such consideration. That being the
only issue to be considered, we set aside not only the
impugned  order  passed  by  the  High  Court  but  also  the
revisional order and the order passed by the Collector dated
31st March, 2008 and remit the matter to the Collector to
take  a  fresh  decision  in  accordance  with  law  after
considering the material on record.  The Collector would be
at liberty to get any fresh inspection to be carried out with
respect to the location of the land in question.
7. The Appeal stands allowed as above.
8. Pending application(s), if any, shall stand disposed of.
………………………………………………………………J.
  [VIKRAM NATH]
………………………………………………………………J.
    [PRASANNA BHALACHANDRA VARALE]
NEW DELHI;
SEPTEMBER 10, 2024

ITEM NO.32               COURT NO.1               SECTION X
               S U P R E M E  C O U R T  O F  I N D I A
                       RECORD OF PROCEEDINGS
SUO MOTO WRIT PETITION(CIVIL)  No(s).  18/2026
IN RE: ENSURING BASIC HUMAN DIGNITY AND SOCIAL SECURITY FOR
DIFFERENTLY ABLED CITIZENS LIVING IN EXTREME POVERTY AND OTHER
ANCILLARY ISSUES
 
Date : 16-06-2026 This petition was called on for hearing today.
CORAM :  HON'BLE THE CHIEF JUSTICE
         HON'BLE MRS. JUSTICE V. MOHANA
(PARTIAL COURT WORKING DAYS BENCH)
For Petitioner(s) : By Courts Motion
                   
For Respondent(s) : Ms. Mithu Jain, AOR
Ms. Shailja Singh, Adv.
Ms. Diksha Arora, Adv. 
          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. Issue notice.
2. Ms. Mithu Jain, learned Advocate on Record accepts notice on
behalf of the State of Odisha.  
3. She reports that a dwelling unit was supposedly allotted to
Smt. Radhika Bhue, mother of the differently abled Japa Bhue. She
further informs that dwelling units were also assigned to two
brothers of Japa Bhue. We are, however, only concerned about the
sustenance and dignified life for Japa Bhue, who has been blind
since birth, and his 80 year old mother, Smt. Radhika Bhue.
Further, the learned counsel has also apprised us that a sum of
Rs.3,500/- per month is paid to Smt. Radhika Bhue as old age
pension and an equal amount of Rs.3,500/- is being paid to her son
Japa Bhue as disability pension, besides free rice under the
1

--- Page 61 ---
Government scheme.
4. Having regard to such submissions, let the State of Odisha
file an affidavit from an officer not below the rank of the
Additional Chief Secretary, detailing the following:
(i) Whether any old age pension has been granted to Smt. Radhika
Bhue and if so, how much is being paid to her and whether all the
arrears have been paid to her?
(ii)  What other social security benefits are available to Smt.
Radhika Bhue, who is prima facie entitled to the same under welfare
schemes formulated by Central or State Government and whether all
the arrears have been paid?
(iii)  Whether Japa Bhue, being a visually impaired person from
birth, has been granted disability pension and whether any such
pension has been granted?
(iv)  Further, what are the other benefits under the social welfare
schemes to which Japa Bhue is entitled, and whether such benefits
have also been granted to him or not?
5. Mr. Aurbindo Pattanaik, Member Secretary of the Odisha State
Legal Services Authority is present online. He is directed to
depute the Secretary of the concerned District Legal Services
Authority to visit the family during the course of the day and
interact with them.  In the event any immediate medical assistance
is required for Smt. Radhika Bhue or her visually impaired son
(Japa Bhue), the District Legal Services Authority of the concerned
District shall, in coordination with the Chief Medical Officer of
the area, make necessary arrangements.
6. Similarly, Japa Bhue, who is a visually impaired person, is
2

--- Page 62 ---
directed to be engaged as a para-legal volunteer, especially for
the purpose of sensitising differently abled persons of their
rights and benefits under various schemes formulated by the Central
and the State Government. On such engagement, Japa Bhue shall be
paid honorarium uninterruptedly and such honorarium shall not be
less than the minimum wages notified by the State of Odisha under
the Minimum Wages Act.
7. The  State  Legal  Services  Authority  shall  also  submit  a
separate report on the social security, namely, the dwelling unit,
if any, allotted to Smt. Radhika Bhue and her son, Japa Bhue. Prima
facie, it appears that Japa Bhue is entitled to a separate dwelling
unit, and this aspect should be especially examined by the State
Legal Services Authority in terms of the Government scheme. If it
is found that he is entitled to such a social security measure, the
matter shall be taken up with the State Government, who shall, in
turn, grant the necessary relief.
8. The State of Odisha and its authorities are directed to ensure
that all basic amenities are made available to Smt. Radhika Bhue
and her son Japa Bhue till further orders.  A status report to this
effect, giving full details of the amenities extended to the mother
and the son, shall be filed.
9. Post this matter for further consideration on 13.07.2026.
(NITIN TALREJA)                              (PREETHI DILEEP KUMAR)
ASTT. REGISTRAR-cum-PS                          DEPUTY REGISTRAR

                       RECORD OF PROCEEDINGS
SPECIAL LEAVE PETITION (CRIMINAL) Diary No(s).25761/2026
[Arising out of impugned final judgment and order dated 27-02-2023
in CRADB No. 518/2014 passed by the High Court of Judicature at
Patna]
SUNIL ROY                                          Petitioner(s)
                                VERSUS
THE STATE OF BIHAR                                 Respondent(s)
IA No. 165191/2026 - CONDONATION OF DELAY IN FILING
 
Date : 15-06-2026 This matter was called on for hearing today.
CORAM : 
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE SANDEEP MEHTA
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE VIJAY BISHNOI
[PARTIAL COURT WORKING DAYS BENCH]
For Petitioner(s) : Ms. Shalini Kaul, AOR
                 
  
For Respondent(s) : 
          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. Delay condoned.
2. The  special  leave  petition  has  been  filed  by  the
petitioner against the judgment dated 27 th February, 2023
passed by the High Court of Judicature at Patna. 
3. By the aforesaid judgment, the High Court dismissed
Criminal Appeal (DB) No. 518 of 2014 and Criminal Appeal (DB)
No. 583 of 2014 preferred by the petitioner and the co-accused
1

--- Page 70 ---
SLP (Crl.) D. No.25761/2026
and upheld the judgment dated 16 th April, 2014 rendered by the
learned Adhoc Additional Sessions Judge-I, Bhojpur, Ara in
Sessions Trial No. 370 of 2012 convicting the accused persons
including the petitioner herein for the offences punishable
under Sections 302 read with Section 34 and Section 307 read
with Section 34 of the Indian Penal Code, 1860 and sentencing
them to suffer imprisonment for life till their natural death
along with fine of Rs.2,00,000/- payable by each accused and
with further punishment for default payment.  For the offence
punishable under Section 307 read with Section 34 of the IPC,
the accused were sentenced to suffer imprisonment for life
along with fine of Rs.1,00,000/- payment by each of them with
further punishment for default payment.
4. While the co-accused Bharath Roy, Uma Shankar Roy alias
Uma Roy and Shakuntla Devi, appear, have not preferred any
special leave petition for assailing their conviction till
date, only the petitioner-Sunil Roy is before us by way of the
instant special leave petition.
5. The case involves brutal murder of five persons, amongst
which two were real brothers of accused No. 1 Bharath Roy, two
were his nephews and one was his sister-in-law.
6. We have considered the submissions of Ms. Shalini Kaul,
learned counsel for the petitioner and gone through the
material placed on record carefully.
7. The case of the prosecution has been well proved by the
ocular testimony of PW-1 Akash Kumar @ Vikky Kumar and PW-4
2

--- Page 71 ---
SLP (Crl.) D. No.25761/2026
Rubi Kumari, both of whom received injuries in the same
incident. 
8. Learned counsel for the petitioner was not in a position
to convince the Court that the reliance placed by the trial
Court and the High Court on the testimony of these two
witnesses was unjustified or that the witnesses were not
present at the spot.  As a matter of fact, the presence of the
witnesses at the spot is well established and corroborated by
the fact that both of them received injuries in the very same
incident.
9. Two competent Courts have recorded concurrent findings of
the facts in convicting the petitioner as well as the co-
accused  and  affirming  their  conviction.   The  judgments
rendered by the Courts below do not suffer from any infirmity
and are rather based on sound and thorough appreciation of
evidence available on record and assign detailed reasons for
arriving at a finding of guilt against the accused persons.
10. In this background, we are not inclined to interfere in
the impugned judgment rendered by the High Court.  The special
leave petition is accordingly dismissed as being devoid of
merit.
11. Pending application(s), if any, shall stand disposed of.
(HARPREET KAUR)                                 (NIDHI WASON)
COURT MASTER (SH)                             ASSISTANT  REGISTRAR

ITEM NO.15               COURT NO.5               SECTION XII-A
               S U P R E M E  C O U R T  O F  I N D I A
                       RECORD OF PROCEEDINGS
PETITION(S) FOR SPECIAL LEAVE TO APPEAL (C)  NO(S).  19870-
19871/2026
[Arising out of impugned final judgment and order dated  02-04-2026
in ARBA No. 101/2025 27-02-2026 in ARBA No. 101/2025 passed by the 
High Court for the State of Telangana at Hyderabad]
BHARTIA INFRA PROJECTS LIMITED                     PETITIONER(S)
                                VERSUS
M/S VISHWA SAMUDRA ENGINEERING PRIVATE LIMITED     RESPONDENT(S)
FOR ADMISSION 
(IA No. 171190/2026 - EXEMPTION FROM FILING O.T.)
 
Date : 15-06-2026 These matters were called on for hearing today.
CORAM :  HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE JOYMALYA BAGCHI
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE VIPUL M. PANCHOLI
(PARTIAL COURT WORKING DAYS BENCH)
For Petitioner(s)  Mr. Ankur Khandelwal, Adv.
                   Mr. Mohd Shahrukh Ali, Adv.
                   Mr. Chirag Sharma, Adv.
                   Mr. Alok Nayak, Adv.
                   Ms. Syed Tabeer Riyaz, AOR
                 
For Respondent(s)  Mr. Prasad Hegde, Adv.
                   Mr. Kailas Bajirao Autade, AOR
                   Mr. B Veera Swamy Raju, Adv.
                   Ms. Siri Swathi Katragadda, Adv.
    UPON hearing the counsel the court made the following
                             O R D E R
1. The petitioner has assailed the judgment and orders
dated  02.04.2026 and 27.02.2026 passed by the Telangana
High Court referring the dispute to arbitration under
Section 11(6) of the Arbitration and Conciliation Act,
1996 (for short ‘the Act’).
2. The short issue which is raised before us is that
1

--- Page 73 ---
SLP (C)  NO(S).  19870-19871/2026
the Telangana High Court did not have jurisdiction to
make such reference and that the Gauhati High Court was
the appropriate forum. The work order had been issued
from Guwahati and the entire work was to be executed
there. As the cause of action had arisen in Guwahati,
petitioner  had  approached  Gauhati  High  Court  for
appointment of arbitrator. Telangana High Court failed to
consider the law laid down in Arif Azim Company Limited
versus Micromax Informatics FZE reported in 2025 (9) SCC
750 and erroneously allowed the Section 11 application,
on the ground that it was filed earlier.
3. We  have  considered  the  aforesaid  submissions.
Relevant arbitration clause reads as follows:
“ARBITRATION: Any dispute, controversy or claim
arising out of or relating to or in connection
with this Agreement, or the breach, termination
or validity hereof shall be finally settled by
arbitration  in  accordance  with  the  Indian
Arbitration & Conciliation Act, 1996 or any
statutory  modification  therein.  Any  dispute
shall be settled by arbitration presided by a
sole arbitrator. The sole arbitrator shall be
an independent person and shall be mutually
appointed by the Parties. The Seat and Venue of
the arbitration shall be Hyderabad, Telangana
state  or  Guwahati,  Assam  state,  and  the
language used in the arbitral proceedings shall
be English. 
This Agreement shall be governed by the laws of
Republic of India and courts in Hyderabad shall
have  exclusive  jurisdiction  over  matters
relating to or arising from this agreement."
4. A holistic reading of the clause would show that
though twin Seat/Venue of arbitration, that is, either
2

--- Page 74 ---
SLP (C)  NO(S).  19870-19871/2026
“Hyderabad, Telangana state or Guwahati, Assam State” is
prescribed,  the  subsequent  part  of  the  clause
unequivocally states that the courts in Hyderabad shall
have exclusive jurisdiction over matters relating to or
arising from this agreement.  In paragraph 77.10 of Arif
Azim Company Limited (supra), a three Judge Bench of this
Court held if two or more possible places are designated
as seat, the principles of  forum non conveniens  would
apply. Such proposition of law though unexceptionable is
inapplicable  in  the  facts  where  the  parties  have
themselves agreed to the exclusive jurisdiction of the
Courts in Hyderabad in the arbitration clause itself.
Party  autonomy  being  of  primary  importance  in
interpretation of the arbitration agreement, we are of
the considered view, the ratio in  Arif Azim Company
Limited  (supra) is factually distinguishable where the
supervisory jurisdiction of the Telangana High Court over
the arbitration is clearly discernible from the clause
itself.
5. In such view of the matter, we are not inclined to
interfere with the impugned orders.
6. The  Special  Leave  Petitions  are  accordingly
dismissed. Pending application(s), if any, shall stand
disposed of.
 (Chetna Balooni)  (Geeta Ahuja)
Court Master (NSH) Deputy Registrar

1. The  instant  writ  petition,  under  Article  32  of  the
Constitution of India, has been filed seeking following reliefs:
a) direct the Centre to implement creamy layer system in
tax exemption for schedule tribes under Section-11 read
with Schedule-III, Sr. No-19 of the Income Tax Act 2025,
in order to ensure that advantage is given to only poor
scheduled tribe individuals, not the rich and elite
class;
b) alternatively, direct and declare that blanket tax
exemption under Section-11, Serial No. 19 of Schedule-
III of the Income-Tax Act, 2025 is manifestly arbitrary,
irrational and violates Articles 14, 15, 19(i)(g), 21,
27 of the Constitution. Hence, void & inoperative;
c) pass such other order(s) as Court deems fit and
1

--- Page 122 ---
proper in facts and circumstances of the case and in the
interest of justice
2. We have heard Shri Ashwini Kumar Upadhyay, petitioner-in-
person, at a considerable length.
3. It seems to us that the reliefs sought in the instant petition
essentially involve formulation, revision, and/or amendment of the
legislative public policy. This Court may not, therefore, be an
appropriate platform for the aforesaid purpose at this stage.
4. The petitioner, if so advised, may approach the Committee on
Petitions, constituted under Rule 306 of the Rules of Procedure and
Conduct of Business in Lok Sabha, by way of a comprehensive
petition.
5. Similarly, the petitioner shall be at liberty to send a copy
of this writ petition, as a representation, to the respondents as
well as other concerned Authorities.

of.

petitioner was dismissed and the order passed by

Petition is delayed by 1377 days.

against  the  petitioner  for  prolonged  and

petitioner  failed  to  report  for  duty  on
absolutely perfunctory grounds.

entertain  the  instant  Special  Leave  Petition,
which is accordingly, dismissed on the ground of
delay as well as on merits.

disposed of.

               S U P R E M E  C O U R T  O F  I N D I A
                       RECORD OF PROCEEDINGS
Petition(s) for Special Leave to Appeal (C)  No(s).  19631/2026
[Arising out of impugned final judgment and order dated  10-03-2026
in WA No. 436/2026 passed by the High Court of Madhya Pradesh at
Gwalior]
SHIROMANI SINGH MAHESHWARI                         Petitioner(s)
                                VERSUS
THE STATE OF MADHYA PRADESH & ORS.                 Respondent(s)
FOR ADMISSION 
IA No. 169912/2026 - EXEMPTION FROM FILING O.T.
 
WITH
SLP(C) No. 21262/2026 (IV-C)
FOR ADMISSION
IA No. 173825/2026 - EXEMPTION FROM FILING O.T.
 
Date : 16-06-2026 These matters were called on for hearing today.
CORAM :  HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE JOYMALYA BAGCHI
         HON'BLE MR. JUSTICE VIPUL M. PANCHOLI
For Petitioner(s) :Mr. S S Pandey, Adv.
                   Mr. Devendra Kumar, Adv.
                   Mr. Raj Kumar, Adv.
                   Mr. Brajesh Chaubey, Adv.
                   Mr. Abhinav Sharma, Adv.
                   Mr. Amrendra Kumar Singh, Adv.
                   Mr. Rakesh Kumar Singh, AOR
                                      
For Respondent(s) : 
          UPON hearing the counsel the Court made the following
                             O R D E R
Special Leave to Appeal (C)  No(s).  19631/2026
1. Learned counsel for the petitioner argues that he ought not to
have non-suited on the ground of delay and laches. He further
submits that materials on record clearly shows that the answer
script had not been correctly assessed. 
2. We have given our anxious consideration to such submission.

--- Page 154 ---
The petitioner who is a constable had appeared in the examination
in the year 2007 and the results were published in the year 2010.
Amended result was published in the year 2011. In 2016 i.e., after
a lapse of six years, the petitioner applied under Right to
Information  (RTI)  for  supply  of  answer  scripts  and  being
dissatisfied approached the Court. No explanation is forthcoming
why the petitioner had not contemporaneously or at least within the
lifetime of the selected panel i.e., one year as per extant rules
applied for supply of answer scripts and taken recourse to law. The
delay on part of the petitioner is substantial and no justifiable
reason has been offered either before the High Court or before us.
The petitioner has to blame himself for the consequence i.e., the
expiration of the panel and the conclusion of the selection process
in the meantime. Under such circumstances, no case for interference
is made out. 
3. The Special Leave Petition is accordingly dismissed and the
accompanying interlocutory application(s), if any, stands disposed
of.  
SLP(C) No. 21262/2026
4. In view of the order passed in SLP (C) No. 19631 of 2026, the 
present Special Leave Petition also stands dismissed. 
5. Pending application(s), if any, shall stand disposed of. 
(KAPIL TANDON)                                (CHETNA BALOONI)
COURT MASTER (SH)                             COURT MASTER (NSH)

2. Delay condoned.
3. Applications  seeking  exemption  from  filing

translation are allowed.
4. Petitioner is aggrieved by the following condition
imposed by the High Court of Punjab & Haryana at
1

--- Page 220 ---
Chandigarh in the impugned order dated 11.11.2025:
“The  vehicle  in  question  is  ordered  to  be
released on furnishing of personal surety bond
in the sum of Rs.1 lakh by the petitioner. All
other conditions shall remain same.”
5. We find that the petitioner is the subsequent
purchaser,  which  was  purchased  from  the  earlier
purchaser, M/s ANI Technologies Pvt. Ltd. (OLA), in the
year 2023 through a public auction. It is alleged that
the vehicle in question was involved in a crime.
6. In such circumstances, the High Court has modified
the order of the Judicial Magistrate First Class,
Rewari directing furnishing of Superdginama in the sum
of Rs.4 lakhs, to the extent to furnishing of personal
surety bond of Rs.1 lakh.
7. We do not find any good reason to interfere with
the order passed by the High Court.
8. Accordingly,  the  Special  Leave  Petition  is
dismissed.
9. Pending  application(s),  if  any,  shall  stand
disposed of.
